style="text-align:center;border-top:#aaa 1px solid"><a href="/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_state_symbols" title="Lists of United States state symbols">Lists of United States state symbols</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Alaska</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Alaska.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/En-us-Alaska.ogg" title="En-us-Alaska.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Aleut_language" title="Aleut language">Aleut</a>: <i lang="ale">Alax&#770;sxax&#770;</i>; <a href="/wiki/Inupiaq_language" title="Inupiaq language">Inupiaq</a>: <i lang="ik">Alaasikaq</i>; <a href="/wiki/Alutiiq_language" title="Alutiiq language">Alutiiq</a>: <i>Alas\'kaaq;</i> <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">&#1040;&#1083;&#1103;&#1089;&#1082;&#1072;</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">translit.</a>&#160;</small><i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language transliteration">Alyaska</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> in the northwest extremity of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, just across the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a> from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">Canadian</a> province of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> and territory of <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a> border the state to the east, its most extreme western part is <a href="/wiki/Attu_Island" title="Attu Island">Attu Island</a>, and it has a maritime border with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chukotka_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Chukotka Autonomous Okrug">Chukotka Autonomous Okrug</a>) to the west across the Bering Strait. To the north are the <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Sea" title="Chukchi Sea">Chukchi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beaufort_Sea" title="Beaufort Sea">Beaufort</a> seas&#8212;southern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> lies to the south and southwest. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">largest state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> by area and the \n<a href="/wiki/List_of_country_subdivisions_by_area" title="List of country subdivisions by area">seventh largest subnational division in the world</a>. In addition, it is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">3rd least populous</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population density">most sparsely populated</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">50 United States</a>; nevertheless, it is by far the most populous territory located mostly north of the <a href="/wiki/60th_parallel_north" title="60th parallel north">60th parallel</a> in North America: its population&#8212;estimated at 738,432 by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> in 2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-5">[5]</a></sup>&#8212; is more than quadruple the combined populations of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Northern Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>. Approximately half of Alaska\'s residents live within the <a href="/wiki/Anchorage_metropolitan_area" title="Anchorage metropolitan area">Anchorage metropolitan area</a>. Alaska\'s economy is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> industries, resources which it has in abundance. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">Military</a> bases and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> are also a significant part of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Alaska" title="Economy of Alaska">economy</a>.\n</p><p>The United States <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Purchase" title="Alaska Purchase">purchased Alaska</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> on March 30, 1867, for 7.2&#160;million U.S. dollars at approximately two cents per acre ($4.74/km<sup>2</sup>).  The area went through several administrative changes before becoming organized as a <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">territory</a> on May 11, 1912. It was admitted as the 49th state of the U.S. on January 3, 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Cities, towns and boroughs</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43"><a href="#Cities_and_census-designated_places_(by_population)"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Cities and census-designated places (by population)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Public_health_and_public_safety"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Public health and public safety</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-47"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#Alaska_in_film_and_on_television"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Alaska in film and on television</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#State_symbols"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">State symbols</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-53"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<p>The name "Alaska" (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">&#1040;&#1083;&#1103;&#1089;&#1082;&#1072;</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">tr.</a></small> <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian language text">Alyaska</i>) was introduced in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian colonial period</a> when it was used to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Peninsula" title="Alaska Peninsula">Alaska Peninsula</a>. It was derived from an <a href="/wiki/Aleut_language" title="Aleut language">Aleut-language</a> <a href="/wiki/Idiom" title="Idiom">idiom</a>, which figuratively refers to the mainland. Literally, it means <i>object to which the action of the sea is directed</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aleut_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aleut-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bright_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bright-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Alaska%22" rel="nofollow">"Alaska"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Alaska%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Alaska%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Alaska%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Alaska%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Alaska%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Alaska" title="Geography of Alaska">Geography of Alaska</a></div>\n<p>Alaska is the northernmost and westernmost state in the United States and has the most easterly longitude in the United States because the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> extend into the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern Hemisphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>  Alaska is the only non-<a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous</a> U.S. state on continental North America; about 500 miles (800&#160;km) of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> (Canada) separates Alaska from <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>. It is technically part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">continental U.S.</a>, but is sometimes not included in colloquial use; Alaska is not part of the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous U.S.</a>, often called <a href="/wiki/Outside_(Alaska)" title="Outside (Alaska)">"the Lower 48"</a>. The capital city, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juneau" title="Juneau">Juneau</a>, is situated on the mainland of the North American continent but is not connected by road to the rest of the North American highway system.\n</p><p>The state is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> in Canada, to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Alaska" title="Gulf of Alaska">Gulf of Alaska</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> to the south and southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Sea" title="Chukchi Sea">Chukchi Sea</a> to the west and the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a> to the north. Alaska\'s territorial waters touch Russia\'s territorial waters in the Bering Strait, as the Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Diomede_Island" title="Big Diomede Island">Big Diomede Island</a> and Alaskan <a href="/wiki/Little_Diomede_Island" title="Little Diomede Island">Little Diomede Island</a> are only 3 miles (4.8&#160;km) apart. Alaska has a longer coastline than all the other U.S. states combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="758" data-file-width="1184" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg/220px-Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg/330px-Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg/440px-Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_area_compared_to_conterminous_US.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alaska\'s size compared with the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">48 contiguous states</a>. (<a href="/wiki/Albers_projection" title="Albers projection">Albers equal-area conic projection</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>Alaska is the largest state in the United States by total area at 663,268 square miles (1,717,856&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), over twice the size of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, the next largest state. Alaska is larger than all but 18 sovereign countries. Counting territorial waters, Alaska is larger than the combined area of the next three largest states: Texas, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>. It is also larger than the combined area of the 22 smallest U.S. states.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h3>\n<p>There are no officially defined borders demarcating the various regions of Alaska, but there are six widely accepted regions:\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Central">South Central</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Central_Alaska" title="South Central Alaska">South Central Alaska</a></div>\n<p>The most populous region of Alaska, containing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anchorage" title="Anchorage">Anchorage</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Matanuska-Susitna_Valley" title="Matanuska-Susitna Valley">Matanuska-Susitna Valley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kenai_Peninsula" title="Kenai Peninsula">Kenai Peninsula</a>. Rural, mostly unpopulated areas south of the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Range" title="Alaska Range">Alaska Range</a> and west of the <a href="/wiki/Wrangell_Mountains" title="Wrangell Mountains">Wrangell Mountains</a> also fall within the definition of South Central, as do the <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a> area and the communities of <a href="/wiki/Cordova,_Alaska" title="Cordova, Alaska">Cordova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valdez,_Alaska" title="Valdez, Alaska">Valdez</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cities_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-cities-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast">Southeast</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Alaska" title="Southeast Alaska">Southeast Alaska</a></div>\n<p>Also referred to as the Panhandle or <a href="/wiki/Inside_Passage" title="Inside Passage">Inside Passage</a>, this is the region of Alaska closest to the rest of the United States. As such, this was where most of the initial non-indigenous settlement occurred in the years following the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Purchase" title="Alaska Purchase">Alaska Purchase</a>. The region is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Archipelago" title="Alexander Archipelago">Alexander Archipelago</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Tongass_National_Forest" title="Tongass National Forest">Tongass National Forest</a>, the largest national forest in the United States. It contains the state capital <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juneau" title="Juneau">Juneau</a>, the former capital <a href="/wiki/Sitka,_Alaska" title="Sitka, Alaska">Sitka</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ketchikan" title="Ketchikan">Ketchikan</a>, at one time Alaska\'s largest city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Marine_Highway" title="Alaska Marine Highway">Alaska Marine Highway</a> provides a vital surface transportation link throughout the area, as only three communities (<a href="/wiki/Haines,_Alaska" title="Haines, Alaska">Haines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyder,_Alaska" title="Hyder, Alaska">Hyder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skagway,_Alaska" title="Skagway, Alaska">Skagway</a>) enjoy direct connections to the contiguous North American road system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOT_Document_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-DOT_Document-14">[14]</a></sup> Officially designated in 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alaska.org_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alaska.org-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Interior">Interior</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Interior" title="Alaska Interior">Alaska Interior</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="303" data-file-width="452" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg/220px-Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg/330px-Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg/440px-Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denali_Mt_McKinley.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Denali" title="Denali">Denali</a> is the highest peak in North America.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Interior is the largest region of Alaska; much of it is uninhabited wilderness. <a href="/wiki/Fairbanks,_Alaska" title="Fairbanks, Alaska">Fairbanks</a> is the only large city in the region. <a href="/wiki/Denali_National_Park_and_Preserve" title="Denali National Park and Preserve">Denali National Park and Preserve</a> is located here. <i><a href="/wiki/Denali" title="Denali">Denali</a></i> is the highest <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountain</a> in North America.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southwest">Southwest</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Alaska" title="Southwest Alaska">Southwest Alaska</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1726" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg/170px-Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg/255px-Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg/340px-Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grizzly_Bear_Fishing_Brooks_Falls.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Grizzly_bear" title="Grizzly bear">Grizzly bear</a> fishing for <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Falls" title="Brooks Falls">Brooks Falls</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/Katmai_National_Park_and_Preserve" title="Katmai National Park and Preserve">Katmai National Park and Preserve</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Southwest Alaska is a sparsely inhabited region stretching some 500 miles (800&#160;km) inland from the Bering Sea. Most of the population lives along the coast. <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak Island</a> is also located in Southwest. The massive <a href="/wiki/Yukon%E2%80%93Kuskokwim_Delta" title="Yukon&#8211;Kuskokwim Delta">Yukon&#8211;Kuskokwim Delta</a>, one of the largest river deltas in the world, is here. Portions of the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Peninsula" title="Alaska Peninsula">Alaska Peninsula</a> are considered part of Southwest, with the remaining portions included with the Aleutian Islands (see below).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Slope">North Slope</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alaska_North_Slope" title="Alaska North Slope">Alaska North Slope</a></div>\n<p>The North Slope is mostly <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> peppered with small villages. The area is known for its massive reserves of crude oil, and contains both the <a href="/wiki/National_Petroleum_Reserve%E2%80%93Alaska" title="National Petroleum Reserve&#8211;Alaska">National Petroleum Reserve&#8211;Alaska</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay_Oil_Field" title="Prudhoe Bay Oil Field">Prudhoe Bay Oil Field</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utqiagvik" title="Utqiagvik">Utqiagvik</a>, formerly known as Barrow, is the northernmost city in the United States and is located here. The <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Arctic_Borough,_Alaska" title="Northwest Arctic Borough, Alaska">Northwest Arctic area</a>, anchored by <a href="/wiki/Kotzebue,_Alaska" title="Kotzebue, Alaska">Kotzebue</a> and also containing the <a href="/wiki/Kobuk_River" title="Kobuk River">Kobuk River</a> valley, is often regarded as being part of this region. However, the respective <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inupiat_people" title="Inupiat people">Inupiat</a> of the North Slope and of the Northwest Arctic seldom consider themselves to be one people<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aleutian_Islands">Aleutian Islands</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a></div>\n<p>More than 300 small volcanic islands make up this chain, which stretches over 1,200 miles (1,900&#160;km) into the Pacific Ocean. Some of these islands fall in the Eastern Hemisphere, but the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a> was drawn west of <a href="/wiki/180th_meridian" title="180th meridian">180&#176;</a> to keep the whole state, and thus the entire North American continent, within the same legal day. Two of the islands, <a href="/wiki/Attu_Island" title="Attu Island">Attu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kiska" title="Kiska">Kiska</a>, were occupied by Japanese forces during World War II.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_features">Natural features</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Alaska" title="Wildlife of Alaska">Wildlife of Alaska</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1361" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg/220px-Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg/330px-Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg/440px-Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Augustine_Volcano_Jan_12_2006_edited-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Augustine_Volcano" title="Augustine Volcano">Augustine Volcano</a> erupting on January 12, 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>With its myriad islands, Alaska has nearly 34,000 miles (55,000&#160;km) of tidal shoreline. The <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> chain extends west from the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Peninsula" title="Alaska Peninsula">Alaska Peninsula</a>. Many active <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a> are found in the Aleutians and in coastal regions. <a href="/wiki/Unimak_Island" title="Unimak Island">Unimak Island</a>, for example, is home to <a href="/wiki/Mount_Shishaldin" title="Mount Shishaldin">Mount Shishaldin</a>, which is an occasionally smoldering volcano that rises to 10,000 feet (3,000&#160;m) above the North Pacific. It is the most perfect volcanic cone on Earth, even more symmetrical than Japan\'s <a href="/wiki/Mount_Fuji" title="Mount Fuji">Mount Fuji</a>. The chain of volcanoes extends to <a href="/wiki/Mount_Spurr" title="Mount Spurr">Mount Spurr</a>, west of Anchorage on the mainland. Geologists have identified Alaska as part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrangellia" title="Wrangellia">Wrangellia</a>, a large region consisting of multiple states and Canadian provinces in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a>, which is actively undergoing <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">continent building</a>.\n</p><p>One of the world\'s largest tides occurs in <a href="/wiki/Turnagain_Arm" title="Turnagain Arm">Turnagain Arm</a>, just south of Anchorage, where tidal differences can be more than 35 feet (10.7&#160;m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_in_Alaska" title="List of lakes in Alaska">List of lakes in Alaska</a></div>\n<p>Alaska has more than three million lakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marshland" title="Marshland">Marshlands</a> and wetland <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a> cover 188,320 square miles (487,700&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) (mostly in northern, western and southwest flatlands). Glacier ice covers about 28,957 square miles (75,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of Alaska.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bering_Glacier" title="Bering Glacier">Bering Glacier</a> is the largest glacier in North America, covering 2,008 square miles (5,200&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_ownership">Land ownership</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Public-Lands-Western-US.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="818" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Public-Lands-Western-US.png/220px-Public-Lands-Western-US.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Public-Lands-Western-US.png/330px-Public-Lands-Western-US.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Public-Lands-Western-US.png/440px-Public-Lands-Western-US.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Public-Lands-Western-US.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alaska has more public land owned by the federal government than any other state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>According to an October 1998 report by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="United States Bureau of Land Management">United States Bureau of Land Management</a>, approximately 65% of Alaska is owned and managed by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">U.S. federal government</a> as public lands, including a multitude of <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Forest" title="United States National Forest">national forests</a>, national parks, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_wildlife_refuge" title="National wildlife refuge">national wildlife refuges</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Of these, the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="Bureau of Land Management">Bureau of Land Management</a> manages 87&#160;million acres (35&#160;million hectares), or 23.8% of the state. The <a href="/wiki/Arctic_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Arctic National Wildlife Refuge">Arctic National Wildlife Refuge</a> is managed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">United States Fish and Wildlife Service</a>. It is the world\'s largest wildlife refuge, comprising 16&#160;million acres (6.5&#160;million hectares).\n</p><p>Of the remaining land area, the state of Alaska owns 101&#160;million acres (41&#160;million hectares), its entitlement under the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Statehood_Act" title="Alaska Statehood Act">Alaska Statehood Act</a>. A portion of that acreage is occasionally ceded to organized boroughs, under the statutory provisions pertaining to newly formed boroughs. Smaller portions are set aside for rural subdivisions and other homesteading-related opportunities. These are not very popular due to the often remote and roadless locations. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska" title="University of Alaska">University of Alaska</a>, as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_grant_university" title="Land grant university">land grant university</a>, also owns substantial acreage which it manages independently.\n</p><p>Another 44&#160;million acres (18&#160;million hectares) are owned by 12 regional, and scores of local, Native corporations created under the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Native_Claims_Settlement_Act" title="Alaska Native Claims Settlement Act">Alaska Native Claims Settlement Act</a> (ANCSA) of 1971. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Native_Regional_Corporation" title="Alaska Native Regional Corporation">Regional Native corporation</a> <a href="/wiki/Doyon,_Limited" title="Doyon, Limited">Doyon, Limited</a> often promotes itself as the largest private landowner in Alaska in advertisements and other communications. Provisions of ANCSA allowing the corporations\' land holdings to be sold on the open market starting in 1991 were repealed before they could take effect. Effectively, the corporations hold title (including subsurface title in many cases, a privilege denied to individual Alaskans) but cannot sell the land. <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Native_Allotment_Act" title="Alaska Native Allotment Act">Individual Native allotments</a> can be and are sold on the open market, however.\n</p><p>Various private interests own the remaining land, totaling about one percent of the state. Alaska is, by a large margin, the state with the smallest percentage of private land ownership when Native corporation holdings are excluded.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Alaska" title="Climate of Alaska">Climate of Alaska</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="990" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/300px-Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/450px-Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/600px-Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen climate types</a> of Alaska.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_climate_regions_USGS.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="418" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alaska_climate_regions_USGS.gif/220px-Alaska_climate_regions_USGS.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alaska_climate_regions_USGS.gif/330px-Alaska_climate_regions_USGS.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Alaska_climate_regions_USGS.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_climate_regions_USGS.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map depicting the climate zones of Alaska.</div></div></div>\n<p>The climate in Southeast Alaska is a mid-latitude <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen climate classification</a>: <i>Cfb</i>) in the southern sections and a subarctic oceanic climate (K&#246;ppen <i>Cfc</i>) in the northern parts. On an annual basis, Southeast is both the wettest and warmest part of Alaska with milder temperatures in the winter and high precipitation throughout the year. Juneau averages over 50&#160;in (130&#160;cm) of precipitation a year, and <a href="/wiki/Ketchikan,_Alaska" title="Ketchikan, Alaska">Ketchikan</a> averages over 150&#160;in (380&#160;cm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> This is also the only region in Alaska in which the average daytime high temperature is above freezing during the winter months.\n</p><p>The climate of <a href="/wiki/Anchorage,_Alaska" title="Anchorage, Alaska">Anchorage</a> and south central Alaska is mild by Alaskan standards due to the region\'s proximity to the seacoast. While the area gets less rain than southeast Alaska, it gets more snow, and days tend to be clearer. On average, <a href="/wiki/Anchorage,_Alaska" title="Anchorage, Alaska">Anchorage</a> receives 16&#160;in (41&#160;cm) of precipitation a year, with around 75&#160;in (190&#160;cm) of snow, although there are areas in the south central which receive far more snow. It is a subarctic climate (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification#GROUP_D:_Continental/microthermal_climate" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen: <i>Dfc</i></a>) due to its brief, cool summers.\n</p><p>The climate of <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Alaska" title="Southwest Alaska">Western Alaska</a> is determined in large part by the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Alaska" title="Gulf of Alaska">Gulf of Alaska</a>. It is a subarctic oceanic climate in the southwest and a continental subarctic climate farther north. The temperature is somewhat moderate considering how far north the area is. This <a href="/wiki/Region" title="Region">region</a> has a tremendous amount of variety in precipitation. An area stretching from the northern side of the Seward Peninsula to the <a href="/wiki/Kobuk_River" title="Kobuk River">Kobuk River</a> valley (i.&#160;e., the region around <a href="/wiki/Kotzebue_Sound" title="Kotzebue Sound">Kotzebue Sound</a>) is technically a <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>, with portions receiving less than 10&#160;in (25&#160;cm) of precipitation annually. On the other extreme, some locations between <a href="/wiki/Dillingham,_Alaska" title="Dillingham, Alaska">Dillingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bethel,_Alaska" title="Bethel, Alaska">Bethel</a> average around 100&#160;in (250&#160;cm) of precipitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AK-YK_Precip_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-AK-YK_Precip-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The climate of the interior of Alaska is subarctic. Some of the highest and lowest temperatures in Alaska occur around the area near <a href="/wiki/Fairbanks,_Alaska" title="Fairbanks, Alaska">Fairbanks</a>. The summers may have temperatures reaching into the 90s &#176;F (the low-to-mid 30s &#176;C), while in the winter, the temperature can fall below &#8722;60&#160;&#176;F (&#8722;51&#160;&#176;C). Precipitation is sparse in the Interior, often less than 10&#160;in (25&#160;cm) a year, but what precipitation falls in the winter tends to stay the entire <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winter</a>.\n</p><p>The highest and lowest recorded temperatures in Alaska are both in the Interior. The highest is 100&#160;&#176;F (38&#160;&#176;C) in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Yukon,_Alaska" title="Fort Yukon, Alaska">Fort Yukon</a> (which is just 8&#160;mi or 13&#160;km inside the arctic circle) on June 27, 1915,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA-All_Hazards_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-All_Hazards-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DRI_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-DRI-26">[26]</a></sup> making Alaska tied with Hawaii as the state with the lowest high temperature in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The lowest official Alaska temperature is &#8722;80&#160;&#176;F (&#8722;62&#160;&#176;C) in <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Creek,_Alaska" title="Prospect Creek, Alaska">Prospect Creek</a> on January 23, 1971,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA-All_Hazards_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-All_Hazards-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DRI_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-DRI-26">[26]</a></sup> one degree above the lowest temperature recorded in continental North America (in <a href="/wiki/Snag,_Yukon" title="Snag, Yukon">Snag, Yukon, Canada</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The climate in the extreme north of Alaska is <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">Arctic</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification#GROUP_E:_Polar_climates" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen: <i>ET</i></a>) with long, very cold winters and short, cool summers. Even in July, the average low temperature in <a href="/wiki/Utqiagvik,_Alaska" title="Utqiagvik, Alaska">Utqiagvik</a> is 34&#160;&#176;F (1&#160;&#176;C).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Precipitation is light in this part of Alaska, with many places averaging less than 10&#160;in (25&#160;cm) per year, mostly as snow which stays on the ground almost the entire year.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto;">\n<caption>Average daily maximum and minimum temperatures for selected locations in Alaska<sup class="reference" Yukon</a></td>\n<td>73/51</td>\n<td>23/10</td>\n<td>&#8722;11/&#8211;27</td>\n<td>&#8722;23/&#8211;33\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Nome,_Alaska" title="Nome, Alaska">Nome</a></td>\n<td>58/46</td>\n<td>14/8</td>\n<td>13/&#8211;2</td>\n<td>&#8722;10/&#8211;19\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Utqiagvik,_Alaska" title="Utqiagvik, Alaska">Utqiagvik</a></td>\n<td>47/34</td>\n<td>08/1</td>\n<td>&#8722;7/&#8211;19</td>\n<td>&#8722;21/&#8211;28\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Alaska" title="Prehistory of Alaska">Prehistory of Alaska</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Alaska" title="History of Alaska">History of Alaska</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonization">Pre-colonization</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Natives" title="Alaska Natives">Alaska Natives</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AlutiiqDancer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2200" data-file-width="1497" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/AlutiiqDancer.jpg/170px-AlutiiqDancer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/AlutiiqDancer.jpg/255px-AlutiiqDancer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/AlutiiqDancer.jpg/340px-AlutiiqDancer.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AlutiiqDancer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alutiiq_people" title="Alutiiq people">Alutiiq</a> dancer in traditional festival garb.</div></div></div>\n<p>Numerous indigenous peoples occupied Alaska for thousands of years before the arrival of European peoples to the area. Linguistic and DNA studies done here have provided evidence for the settlement of North America by way of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bering_land_bridge" title="Bering land bridge">Bering land bridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Upward_Sun_River_site" title="Upward Sun River site">Upward Sun River site</a> in the Tanana River Valley in Alaska, remains of a six-week-old infant were found. The baby\'s DNA showed that she belonged to a population that was genetically separate from other native groups present elsewhere in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a>. Ben Potter, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska_Fairbanks" title="University of Alaska Fairbanks">University of Alaska Fairbanks</a> archaeologist who unearthed the remains at the Upward River Sun site in 2013, named this new group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Beringians" title="Ancient Beringians">Ancient Beringians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tlingit_people" title="Tlingit people">Tlingit people</a> developed a society with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrilineal" title="Matrilineal">matrilineal</a> kinship system of property inheritance and descent in what is today Southeast Alaska, along with parts of British Columbia and the Yukon. Also in Southeast were the <a href="/wiki/Haida_people" title="Haida people">Haida</a>, now well known for their unique arts. The <a href="/wiki/Tsimshian" title="Tsimshian">Tsimshian</a> people came to Alaska from British Columbia in 1887, when President <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a>, and later the U.S. Congress, granted them permission to settle on <a href="/wiki/Annette_Island" title="Annette Island">Annette Island</a> and found the town of <a href="/wiki/Metlakatla,_Alaska" title="Metlakatla, Alaska">Metlakatla</a>. All three of these peoples, as well as other <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Pacific_Northwest_Coast" title="Indigenous peoples of the Pacific Northwest Coast">indigenous peoples of the Pacific Northwest Coast</a>, experienced <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> outbreaks from the late 18th through the mid-19th century, with the most devastating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epidemics" title="Epidemics">epidemics</a> occurring in the 1830s and 1860s, resulting in high fatalities and social disruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Aleutian Islands are still home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleut_people" title="Aleut people">Aleut people</a>\'s seafaring society, although they were the first Native Alaskans to be exploited by Russians. Western and Southwestern Alaska are home to the <a href="/wiki/Yup%27ik" title="Yup\'ik">Yup\'ik</a>, while their cousins the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alutiiq_people" title="Alutiiq people">Alutiiq ~ Sugpiaq</a> lived in what is now Southcentral Alaska. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwich%27in_people" title="Gwich\'in people">Gwich\'in people</a> of the northern Interior region are <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Athabaskans" title="Alaskan Athabaskans">Athabaskan</a> and primarily known today for their dependence on the caribou within the much-contested <a href="/wiki/Arctic_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Arctic National Wildlife Refuge">Arctic National Wildlife Refuge</a>. The North Slope and <a href="/wiki/Little_Diomede_Island" title="Little Diomede Island">Little Diomede Island</a> are occupied by the widespread <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inupiat_people" title="Inupiat people">Inupiat people</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonization">Colonization</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Alaska" title="Department of Alaska">Department of Alaska</a>, and <a href="/wiki/District_of_Alaska" title="District of Alaska">District of Alaska</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1860-russian-america.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="831" data-file-width="732" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1860-russian-america.jpg/170px-1860-russian-america.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1860-russian-america.jpg/255px-1860-russian-america.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1860-russian-america.jpg/340px-1860-russian-america.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1860-russian-america.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Russian America in 1860</div></div></div>\n<p>Some researchers believe that the first Russian settlement in Alaska was established in the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> According to this hypothesis, in 1648 several <a href="/wiki/Koch_(boat)" title="Koch (boat)">koches</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a>\'s expedition came ashore in Alaska by storm and founded this settlement. This hypothesis is based on the testimony of <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_people" title="Chukchi people">Chukchi</a> geographer <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nikolai_Daurkin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nikolai Daurkin (page does not exist)">Nikolai Daurkin</a>, who had visited Alaska in 1764&#8211;1765 and who had reported on a village on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kheuveren&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kheuveren (page does not exist)">Kheuveren</a> River, populated by "bearded men" who "pray to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icons" title="Icons">icons</a>". Some modern researchers associate Kheuveren with <a href="/wiki/Koyuk_River" title="Koyuk River">Koyuk River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first European vessel to reach Alaska is generally held to be the <i>St. Gabriel</i> under the authority of the surveyor <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gvozdev" title="Mikhail Gvozdev">M. S. Gvozdev</a> and assistant navigator <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Fyodorov_(navigator)" title="Ivan Fyodorov (navigator)">I. Fyodorov</a> on August 21, 1732, during an expedition of Siberian cossak <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Afanasiy_Shestakov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Afanasiy Shestakov (page does not exist)">A. F. Shestakov</a> and Belarusian explorer <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Pavlutsky" title="Dmitry Pavlutsky">Dmitry Pavlutsky</a> (1729&#8211;1735).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another European contact with Alaska occurred in 1741, when <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a> led an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Kamchatka_expedition" title="Second Kamchatka expedition">expedition</a> for the Russian Navy aboard the <i>St. Peter</i>. After his crew returned to Russia with <a href="/wiki/Sea_otter" title="Sea otter">sea otter</a> pelts judged to be the finest fur in the world, small associations of fur traders began to sail from the shores of Siberia toward the Aleutian Islands. The first permanent European settlement was founded in 1784.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1267" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg/220px-Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg/330px-Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg/440px-Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Russian settlement of St. Paul\'s Harbor (present-day <a href="/wiki/Kodiak,_Alaska" title="Kodiak, Alaska">Kodiak town</a>), <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak Island</a>, 1814.</div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1774 and 1800, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">Spain</a> sent several <a href="/wiki/Spanish_expeditions_to_the_Pacific_Northwest" title="Spanish expeditions to the Pacific Northwest">expeditions to Alaska</a> in order to assert its claim over the Pacific Northwest. In 1789 a Spanish settlement and <a href="/wiki/Fort_San_Miguel" title="Fort San Miguel">fort</a> were built in <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Sound" title="Nootka Sound">Nootka Sound</a>. These expeditions gave names to places such as <a href="/wiki/Valdez,_Alaska" title="Valdez, Alaska">Valdez</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bucareli_Sound" title="Bucareli Sound">Bucareli Sound</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cordova,_Alaska" title="Cordova, Alaska">Cordova</a>. Later, the <a href="/wiki/Russian-American_Company" title="Russian-American Company">Russian-American Company</a> carried out an expanded colonization program during the early-to-mid-19th century.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sitka,_Alaska" title="Sitka, Alaska">Sitka</a>, renamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Archangel" title="New Archangel">New Archangel</a> from 1804 to 1867, on <a href="/wiki/Baranof_Island" title="Baranof Island">Baranof Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Archipelago" title="Alexander Archipelago">Alexander Archipelago</a> in what is now <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Alaska" title="Southeast Alaska">Southeast Alaska</a>, became the capital of <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian America</a>. It remained the capital after the colony was transferred to the United States. The Russians never fully colonized Alaska, and the colony was never very profitable. Evidence of Russian settlement in names and churches survive throughout southeast Alaska.\n</p><p>On March 30, 1867, the United States purchased Alaska from the Russian Empire for the sum of $7.2 million. It was not until October of that year that the commissioners arrived in Sitka and the formal transfer was arranged. The formal flag-raising took place at Fort Sitka on October 18, 1867. The original ceremony included 250 uniformed U.S. soldiers, who marched to the governor\'s house at "Castle Hill". Here the Russian troops lowered the Russian flag and the U.S. flag was raised. This event is celebrated as <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Day" title="Alaska Day">Alaska Day</a>, a legal holiday on the 18th of October.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/William_H._Seward" title="William H. Seward">William H. Seward</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a>, negotiated the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Purchase" title="Alaska Purchase">Alaska Purchase</a> (also known as Seward\'s Folly) with the Russians in 1867 for $7.2&#160;million. Alaska was loosely governed by the military initially, and was administered as a <a href="/wiki/District_of_Alaska" title="District of Alaska">district</a> starting in 1884, with a governor appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>. A federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_territorial_court" title="United States territorial court">district court</a> was headquartered in Sitka.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1994" data-file-width="2536" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg/220px-Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg/330px-Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg/440px-Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miners_climb_Chilkoot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Miners and prospectors climb the <a href="/wiki/Chilkoot_Trail" title="Chilkoot Trail">Chilkoot Trail</a> during the 1898 <a href="/wiki/Klondike_Gold_Rush" title="Klondike Gold Rush">Klondike Gold Rush</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>For most of Alaska\'s first decade under the United States flag, Sitka was the only community inhabited by American settlers. They organized a "provisional city government", which was Alaska\'s first municipal government, but not in a legal sense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Legislation allowing Alaskan communities to legally incorporate as cities did not come about until 1900, and <a href="/wiki/Home_rule#Home_rule_in_the_United_States" title="Home rule">home rule</a> for cities was extremely limited or unavailable until statehood took effect in 1959.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territory">Territory</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Organic_act#List_of_organic_acts" title="Organic act">Organic act &#167;&#160;List of organic acts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Alaska" title="Territory of Alaska">Territory of Alaska</a></div>\n<p>Starting in the 1890s and stretching in some places to the early 1910s, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Gold_Rush" title="Alaska Gold Rush">gold rushes</a> in Alaska and the nearby <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon Territory</a> brought thousands of miners and settlers to Alaska. Alaska was officially incorporated as an organized territory in 1912. Alaska\'s capital, which had been in <a href="/wiki/Sitka,_Alaska" title="Sitka, Alaska">Sitka</a> until 1906, was moved north to <a href="/wiki/Juneau,_Alaska" title="Juneau, Alaska">Juneau</a>. Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Governor%27s_Mansion" title="Alaska Governor\'s Mansion">Alaska Governor\'s Mansion</a> began that same year. European immigrants from Norway and Sweden also settled in southeast Alaska, where they entered the fishing and logging industries.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_troops_at_the_Battle_of_Attu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="337" data-file-width="351" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/US_troops_at_the_Battle_of_Attu.jpg/220px-US_troops_at_the_Battle_of_Attu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/US_troops_at_the_Battle_of_Attu.jpg/330px-US_troops_at_the_Battle_of_Attu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a8/US_troops_at_the_Battle_of_Attu.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_troops_at_the_Battle_of_Attu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. troops navigate snow and ice during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Attu" title="Battle of Attu">Battle of Attu</a> in May 1943.</div></div></div>\n<p>During World War II, the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands_Campaign" title="Aleutian Islands Campaign">Aleutian Islands Campaign</a> focused on the three outer Aleutian Islands &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Attu_Island" title="Attu Island">Attu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agattu" title="Agattu">Agattu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kiska_Island" title="Kiska Island">Kiska</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> &#8211; that were invaded by Japanese troops and occupied between June 1942 and August 1943. During the occupation, one <a href="/wiki/Aleut" title="Aleut">Aleut</a> civilian was killed by Japanese troops and nearly fifty were interned in Japan, where about half of them died.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unalaska" title="Unalaska">Unalaska</a>/<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Harbor" title="Dutch Harbor">Dutch Harbor</a> became a significant base for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">United States Army Air Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submariners</a>.\n</p><p>The United States <a href="/wiki/Lend-Lease" title="Lend-Lease">Lend-Lease</a> program involved the flying of American warplanes through Canada to Fairbanks and then Nome; Soviet pilots took possession of these aircraft, ferrying them to fight the German invasion of the Soviet Union. The construction of military bases contributed to the population growth of some Alaskan cities.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statehood">Statehood</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Statehood_Act" title="Alaska Statehood Act">Alaska Statehood Act</a>, <a href="/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union" title="Admission to the Union">Admission to the Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_date_of_admission_to_the_Union" title="List of U.S. states by date of admission to the Union">List of U.S. states by date of admission to the Union</a></div>\n<p>Statehood for Alaska was an important cause of <a href="/wiki/James_Wickersham" title="James Wickersham">James Wickersham</a> early in his tenure as a congressional delegate. Decades later, the statehood movement gained its first real momentum following a territorial referendum in 1946. The Alaska Statehood Committee and Alaska\'s Constitutional Convention would soon follow. Statehood supporters also found themselves fighting major battles against political foes, mostly in the U.S. Congress but also within Alaska. Statehood was approved by Congress on July 7, 1958. Alaska was officially proclaimed a state on January 3, 1959.\n</p><p>In 1960, the Census Bureau reported Alaska\'s population as 77.2% White, 3% Black, and 18.8% American Indian and Alaska Native.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3628" data-file-width="2293" decoding="async" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg/170px-1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg/255px-1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg/340px-1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1964_Alaska_Quake_Kodiak_Before_and_After.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kodiak, before and after the <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> which followed the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a> earthquake in 1964, destroying much of the townsite.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Good_Friday_earthquake">Good Friday earthquake</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1964_Alaska_earthquake" title="1964 Alaska earthquake">1964 Alaska earthquake</a></div>\n<p>On March 27, 1964, the massive <a href="/wiki/1964_Alaska_earthquake" title="1964 Alaska earthquake">Good Friday earthquake</a> killed 133 people and destroyed several villages and portions of large coastal communities, mainly by the resultant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsunamis" title="Tsunamis">tsunamis</a> and landslides. It was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_earthquakes_by_magnitude" title="Largest earthquakes by magnitude">second-most-powerful earthquake</a> in the recorded history of the world, with a <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">moment magnitude</a> of 9.2. It was over one thousand times more powerful than the <a href="/wiki/1989_Loma_Prieta_earthquake" title="1989 Loma Prieta earthquake">1989 San Francisco earthquake</a>. The time of day (5:36&#160;pm), time of year and location of the epicenter were all cited as factors in potentially sparing thousands of lives, particularly in Anchorage.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_of_oil">Discovery of oil</span></h3>\n<p>The 1968 discovery of oil at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay" title="Prudhoe Bay">Prudhoe Bay</a> and the 1977 completion of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System" title="Trans-Alaska Pipeline System">Trans-Alaska Pipeline System</a> led to an oil boom. Royalty revenues from oil have funded large state budgets from 1980 onward. That same year, not coincidentally, Alaska repealed its state income tax.\n</p><p>In 1989, the <i><a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez" title="Exxon Valdez">Exxon Valdez</a></i> hit a reef in the <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">spilling</a> over 11 million U.S. gallons (42 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalitre" title="Megalitre">megaliters</a>) of crude oil over 1,100 miles (1,800&#160;km) of coastline. Today, the battle between philosophies of development and conservation is seen in the contentious debate over oil drilling in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Arctic National Wildlife Refuge">Arctic National Wildlife Refuge</a> and the proposed <a href="/wiki/Pebble_Mine" title="Pebble Mine">Pebble Mine</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alaska_Heritage_Resources_Survey">Alaska Heritage Resources Survey</span></h3>\n<p>The Alaska Heritage Resources Survey (AHRS) is a restricted <a href="/wiki/Inventory" title="Inventory">inventory</a> of all reported <a href="/wiki/Historic_site" title="Historic site">historic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric" title="Prehistoric">prehistoric</a> sites within the state of Alaska; it is maintained by the Office of History and Archaeology. The survey\'s inventory of cultural resources includes objects, structures, buildings, sites, districts, and travel ways, with a general provision that they are over 50 years old. As of  January&#160;31, 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, over 35,000 sites have been reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Alaska" title="Demographics of Alaska">Demographics of Alaska</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="border-spacing: 1px; float: right; clear: right; margin: 0 0 1em href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Alaska was 738,432 on July 1, 2015, a 3.97% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, Alaska ranked as the 47th state by population, ahead of <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-5">[5]</a></sup> Estimates show North  Dakota  ahead as of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Alaska is the least densely populated state, and one of the most sparsely populated areas in the world, at 1.2 inhabitants per square mile (0.46/km<sup>2</sup>), with the next state, Wyoming, at 5.8 inhabitants per square mile (2.2/km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Alaska is the largest U.S. state by <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">area</a>, and the tenth wealthiest (per capita income).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> As of  November&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the state\'s unemployment rate was 6.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\nAs of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it is one of 14 U.S. states that still has only one telephone <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">area code</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_area_codes_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_area_codes-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_and_Ethnicity">Race and Ethnicity</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="267" data-file-width="463" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg/220px-Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg/330px-Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg/440px-Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alaska_racial_and_ethnic_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the largest racial/ethnic group by borough. Red indicates Native American, blue indicates non-Hispanic white, and green indicates Asian. Darker shades indicate a higher proportion of the population.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, Alaska, had a population of 710,231. In terms of race and ethnicity, the state was 66.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a> (64.1% Non-Hispanic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">White</a>), 14.8% <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a> and Alaska Native, 5.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a>, 3.3% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">Black</a> or African American, 1.0% Native Hawaiian and Other Pacific Islander, 1.6% from Some Other Race, and 7.3% from Two or More Races. <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanics</a> or Latinos of any race made up 5.5% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 50.7% of Alaska\'s population younger than one year of age belonged to minority groups (i.e., did not have two parents of non-Hispanic white ancestry).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable collapsible">\n<caption><b>Alaska racial breakdown of population</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Racial composition</th>\n<th>1970<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-50">[50]</a></sup></th>\n<th>1990<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-census-50">[50]</a></sup></th>\n<th>2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></th>\n<th>2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White
