<i>122,640</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b>54.8%</b> <i>164,676</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Alaska,_2016" title="United States presidential election in Alaska, 2016">2016</a>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF">36.6% <i>116,454</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b>51.3%</b> <i>163,387</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="841" data-file-width="1402" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png/220px-Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png/330px-Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png/440px-Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presidential_vote_in_Alaska.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A line graph showing the presidential vote by party from 1960 to 2016 in Alaska.</div></div></div>\n<p>Alaska regularly supports <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> in presidential elections and has done so since statehood. Republicans have won the state\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral college</a> votes in all but one election that it has participated in (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1964" title="United States presidential election, 1964">1964</a>). No state has voted for a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> presidential candidate fewer times. Alaska was carried by Democratic nominee <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> during his landslide election in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_1964" title="U.S. presidential election, 1964">1964</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_1960" title="U.S. presidential election, 1960">1960</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_1968" title="U.S. presidential election, 1968">1968</a> elections were close. Since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_1972" title="U.S. presidential election, 1972">1972</a>, however, Republicans have carried the state by large margins. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2008" title="U.S. presidential election, 2008">2008</a>, Republican <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> defeated Democrat <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in Alaska, 59.49% to 37.83%. McCain\'s running mate was <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Palin" title="Sarah Palin">Sarah Palin</a>, the state\'s governor and the first Alaskan on a major party ticket. Obama lost Alaska again in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2012" title="U.S. presidential election, 2012">2012</a>, but he captured 40% of the state\'s vote in that election, making him the first Democrat to do so since 1968.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/The_Bush_(Alaska)" title="The Bush (Alaska)">Alaska Bush</a>, central Juneau, midtown and downtown Anchorage, and the areas surrounding the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska_Fairbanks" title="University of Alaska Fairbanks">University of Alaska Fairbanks</a> campus and Ester have been strongholds of the Democratic Party. The Matanuska-Susitna Borough, the majority of Fairbanks (including North Pole and the military base), and South Anchorage typically have the strongest Republican showing. As of  2004<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, well over half of all registered voters have chosen "Non-Partisan" or "Undeclared" as their affiliation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> despite recent attempts to close primaries to unaffiliated voters.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Voter Registration and Party Enrollment as of  July&#160;3, 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2">Party\n</th>\n<th>Number of Voters\n</th>\n<th>Percentage\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#DDDDDD;" width="10px">\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Independent_voter" title="Independent voter">Unaffiliated</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">299,365\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">55.25%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#E81B23;" width="10px">\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">139,615\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">25.77%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#3333FF;" width="10px">\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">74,865\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">13.82%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#FFC14E;" width="10px">\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Independence_Party" title="Alaskan Independence Party">AKIP</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">17,118\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">3.16%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#FED105;" width="10px">\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_(United_States)" title="Libertarian Party (United States)">Libertarian</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">7,422\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1.37%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#DDDDDD;" width="10px">\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_States" title="List of political parties in the United States">Other</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">3,436\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">0.36%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Total\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">541,821\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">100%\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Because of its population relative to other U.S. states, Alaska has only one member in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a>. This seat is held by Republican <a href="/wiki/Don_Young" title="Don Young">Don Young</a>, who was re-elected to his 21st consecutive term in 2012. <a href="/wiki/Alaska%27s_at-large_congressional_district" title="Alaska\'s at-large congressional district">Alaska\'s at-large congressional district</a> is one of the largest parliamentary constituencies in the world by area.\n</p><p>In 2008, Governor <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Palin" title="Sarah Palin">Sarah Palin</a> became the first Republican woman to run on a national ticket when she became <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>\'s running mate. She continued to be a prominent national figure even after resigning from the governor\'s job in July 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Senators_from_Alaska" title="List of United States Senators from Alaska">Alaska\'s United States Senators</a> belong to <a href="/wiki/Classes_of_United_States_Senators" title="Classes of United States Senators">Class 2 and Class 3</a>. In 2008, Democrat <a href="/wiki/Mark_Begich" title="Mark Begich">Mark Begich</a>, mayor of Anchorage, defeated long-time Republican senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Stevens" title="Ted Stevens">Ted Stevens</a>. Stevens had been convicted on seven felony counts of failing to report gifts on Senate financial discloser forms one week before the election. The conviction was set aside in April 2009 after evidence of prosecutorial misconduct emerged.\n</p><p>Republican <a href="/wiki/Frank_Murkowski" title="Frank Murkowski">Frank Murkowski</a> held the state\'s other senatorial position. After being elected governor in 2002, he resigned from the Senate and appointed his daughter, State Representative <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Murkowski" title="Lisa Murkowski">Lisa Murkowski</a> as his successor. She won full six-year terms in 2004, 2010 and 2016.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerycaption">Alaska\'s current statewide elected officials</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" data-file-height="1643" data-file-width="2464" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/CordovaHillside.jpg/180px-CordovaHillside.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Downtown_Talkeetna.jpg/360px-Downtown_Talkeetna.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Talkeetna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main Street in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talkeetna" title="Talkeetna">Talkeetna</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Alaska is not divided into <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>, as most of the other U.S. states, but it is divided into <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_boroughs_and_census_areas_in_Alaska" title="List of boroughs and census areas in Alaska">boroughs</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Many of the more densely populated parts of the state are part of Alaska\'s 16 boroughs, which function somewhat similarly to counties in other states. However, unlike county-equivalents in the other 49 states, the boroughs do not cover the entire land area of the state. The area not part of any borough is referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Unorganized_Borough,_Alaska" title="Unorganized Borough, Alaska">Unorganized Borough</a>.\n</p><p>The Unorganized Borough has no government of its own, but the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a> in cooperation with the state divided the Unorganized Borough into 11 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Census_area" title="Census area">census areas</a> solely for the purposes of statistical analysis and presentation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A <i>recording district</i> is a mechanism for administration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_record" title="Public record">public record</a> in Alaska. The state is divided into 34 recording districts which are centrally administered under a State <a href="/wiki/Recorder_of_deeds" title="Recorder of deeds">Recorder</a>. All recording districts use the same acceptance criteria, fee schedule, etc., for accepting documents into the public record.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Whereas many U.S. states use a three-tiered system of decentralization&#8212;state/county/township&#8212;most of Alaska uses only two tiers&#8212;state/borough. Owing to the low population density, most of the land is located in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unorganized_Borough" title="Unorganized Borough">Unorganized Borough</a>. As the name implies, it has no intermediate borough government but is administered directly by the state government. In 2000, 57.71% of Alaska\'s area has this status, with 13.05% of the population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Anchorage merged the city government with the Greater Anchorage Area Borough in 1975 to form the Municipality of Anchorage, containing the city proper and the communities of Eagle River, Chugiak, Peters Creek, Girdwood, Bird, and Indian. Fairbanks has a separate borough (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fairbanks_North_Star_Borough" title="Fairbanks North Star Borough">Fairbanks North Star Borough</a>) and municipality (the City of Fairbanks).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The state\'s most populous city is <a href="/wiki/Anchorage,_Alaska" title="Anchorage, Alaska">Anchorage</a>, home to 278,700 people in 2006, 225,744 of whom live in the urbanized area. The richest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Alaska locations by per capita income">location in Alaska by per capita income</a> is <a href="/wiki/Halibut_Cove,_Alaska" title="Halibut Cove, Alaska">Halibut Cove</a> ($89,895).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yakutat_City" title="Yakutat City">Yakutat City</a>, Sitka, Juneau, and Anchorage are the four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._cities_by_area" title="List of U.S. cities by area">largest cities in the U.S. by area</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Cities_and_census-designated_places_.28by_population.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_census-designated_places_(by_population)">Cities and census-designated places (by population)</span></h3>\n<p>As reflected in the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, Alaska has a total of 355 incorporated cities and <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated places</a> (CDPs).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>  The tally of cities includes four unified municipalities, essentially the equivalent of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consolidated_city%E2%80%93county" title="Consolidated city&#8211;county">consolidated city&#8211;county</a>. The majority of these communities are located in the rural expanse of Alaska known as "<a href="/wiki/The_Bush_(Alaska)" title="The Bush (Alaska)">The Bush</a>" and are unconnected to the contiguous North American road network. The table at the bottom of this section lists the 100 largest cities and census-designated places in Alaska, in population order.\n</p><p>Of Alaska\'s 2010 Census population figure of 710,231, 20,429 people, or 2.88% of the population, did not live in an incorporated city or census-designated place. Approximately three-quarters of that figure were people who live in urban and suburban neighborhoods on the outskirts of the city limits of Ketchikan, Kodiak, Palmer and Wasilla.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>  CDPs have not been established for these areas by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a>, except that seven CDPs were established for the Ketchikan-area neighborhoods in the <a href="/wiki/1980_United_States_Census" title="1980 United States Census">1980 Census</a> (Clover Pass, Herring Cove, Ketchikan East, Mountain Point, North <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tongass_Highway" title="Tongass Highway">Tongass Highway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennock_Island" title="Pennock Island">Pennock Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saxman,_Alaska" title="Saxman, Alaska">Saxman</a> East), but have not been used since. The remaining population was scattered throughout Alaska, both within organized boroughs and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unorganized_Borough" title="Unorganized Borough">Unorganized Borough</a>, in largely remote areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>No.</th>\n<th>Community name</th>\n<th>Type</th>\n<th><a style="text-align:right;">813\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>79</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Emmonak,_Alaska" title="Emmonak, Alaska">Emmonak</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">762\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>80</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hoonah,_Alaska" title="Hoonah, Alaska">Hoonah</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">760\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>81</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Klawock,_Alaska" title="Klawock, Alaska">Klawock</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">755\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>82</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Moose_Creek,_Alaska" title="Moose Creek, Alaska">Moose Creek</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">747\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>83</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Knik_River,_Alaska" title="Knik River, Alaska">Knik River</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">744\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>84</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Pleasant_Valley,_Alaska" title="Pleasant Valley, Alaska">Pleasant Valley</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">725\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>85</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Kwethluk,_Alaska" title="Kwethluk, Alaska">Kwethluk</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">721\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="2">86</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Two_Rivers,_Alaska" title="Two Rivers, Alaska">Two Rivers</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td rowspan="2" Bay</a></td>\n<td>CDP\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>88</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Unalakleet,_Alaska" title="Unalakleet, Alaska">Unalakleet</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">688\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>89</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Fox_River,_Alaska" title="Fox River, Alaska">Fox River</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">685\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>90</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gambell,_Alaska" title="Gambell, Alaska">Gambell</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">681\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>91</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Alakanuk,_Alaska" title="Alakanuk, Alaska">Alakanuk</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">677\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>92</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Point_Hope,_Alaska" title="Point Hope, Alaska">Point Hope</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">674\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>93</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Savoonga,_Alaska" title="Savoonga, Alaska">Savoonga</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">671\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>94</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Quinhagak,_Alaska" title="Quinhagak, Alaska">Quinhagak</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">669\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>95</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Noorvik,_Alaska" title="Noorvik, Alaska">Noorvik</a></td>\n<td>City</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">668\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>96</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Yakutat,_Alaska" title="Yakutat, Alaska">Yakutat</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">662\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>97</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Kipnuk,_Alaska" title="Kipnuk, Alaska">Kipnuk</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">639\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>98</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Akiachak,_Alaska" title="Akiachak, Alaska">Akiachak</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">627\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>99</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Happy_Valley,_Alaska" title="Happy Valley, Alaska">Happy Valley</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">593\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>100</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Big_Delta,_Alaska" title="Big Delta, Alaska">Big Delta</a></td>\n<td>CDP</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">591\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kachcampus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1396" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Kachcampus.jpg/220px-Kachcampus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Kachcampus.jpg/330px-Kachcampus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Kachcampus.jpg/440px-Kachcampus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kachcampus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kachemak_Bay_Campus" title="Kachemak Bay Campus">Kachemak Bay Campus</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska_Anchorage" title="University of Alaska Anchorage">University of Alaska Anchorage</a>, located in downtown Homer.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Department_of_Education_and_Early_Development" title="Alaska Department of Education and Early Development">Alaska Department of Education and Early Development</a> administers many <a href="/wiki/List_of_school_districts_in_Alaska" title="List of school districts in Alaska">school districts</a> in Alaska. In addition, the state operates a boarding school, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt._Edgecumbe_High_School" title="Mt. Edgecumbe High School">Mt. Edgecumbe High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sitka,_Alaska" title="Sitka, Alaska">Sitka</a>, and provides partial funding for other boarding schools, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nenana_Student_Living_Center" title="Nenana Student Living Center">Nenana Student Living Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nenana,_Alaska" title="Nenana, Alaska">Nenana</a> and The Galena Interior Learning Academy in <a href="/wiki/Galena,_Alaska" title="Galena, Alaska">Galena</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are more than a dozen <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Alaska" title="List of colleges and universities in Alaska">colleges and universities in Alaska</a>. Accredited universities in Alaska include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska_Anchorage" title="University of Alaska Anchorage">University of Alaska Anchorage</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska_Fairbanks" title="University of Alaska Fairbanks">University of Alaska Fairbanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska_Southeast" title="University of Alaska Southeast">University of Alaska Southeast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Pacific_University" title="Alaska Pacific University">Alaska Pacific University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> Alaska is the only state that has no institutions that are part of <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a>.\n</p><p>The Alaska Department of Labor and Workforce Development operates AVTEC, Alaska\'s Institute of Technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Campuses in Seward and Anchorage offer 1 week to 11-month training programs in areas as diverse as Information Technology, Welding, Nursing, and Mechanics.\n</p><p>Alaska has had a problem with a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_drain" title="Brain drain">brain drain</a>". Many of its young people, including most of the highest academic achievers, leave the state after high school graduation and do not return. As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alaska&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Alaska did not have a <a href="/wiki/Legal_education_in_Alaska" title="Legal education in Alaska">law school</a> or medical school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Alaska" title="University of Alaska">University of Alaska</a> has attempted to combat this by offering partial four-year scholarships to the top 10% of Alaska high school graduates, via the Alaska Scholars Program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_health_and_public_safety">Public health and public safety</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dentistry_in_rural_Alaska" title="Dentistry in rural Alaska">Dentistry in rural Alaska</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alaska_State_Troopers" title="Alaska State Troopers">Alaska State Troopers</a> are Alaska\'s statewide police force. They have a long and storied history, but were not an official organization until 1941. Before the force was officially organized, law enforcement in Alaska was handled by various federal agencies. Larger towns usually have their own local police and some villages rely on "Public Safety Officers" who have police training but do not carry firearms. In much of the state, the troopers serve as the only police force available. In addition to enforcing traffic and criminal law, wildlife Troopers enforce hunting and fishing regulations. Due to the varied terrain and wide scope of the Troopers\' duties, they employ a wide variety of land, air, and water patrol vehicles.\n</p><p>Many rural communities in Alaska are considered "dry", having outlawed the importation of alcoholic beverages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> Suicide rates for rural residents are higher than urban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_abuse" title="Domestic abuse">Domestic abuse</a> and other violent crimes are also at high levels in the state; this is in part linked to alcohol abuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> Alaska has the highest rate of sexual assault in the nation, especially in rural areas. The average age of sexually assaulted victims is 16 years old. In four out of five cases, the suspects were relatives, friends or acquaintances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_artists_and_writers_from_Alaska" title="List of artists and writers from Alaska">List of artists and writers from Alaska</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage,_Alaska.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2001" data-file-width="2921" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage%2C_Alaska.jpg/220px-Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage%2C_Alaska.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage%2C_Alaska.jpg/330px-Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage%2C_Alaska.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage%2C_Alaska.jpg/440px-Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage%2C_Alaska.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iditarod_Ceremonial_start_in_Anchorage,_Alaska.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A dog team in the <a href="/wiki/Iditarod_Trail_Sled_Dog_Race" title="Iditarod Trail Sled Dog Race">Iditarod Trail Sled Dog Race</a>, arguably the most popular winter event in Alaska.</div></div></div>\n<p>Some of Alaska\'s popular annual events are the <a href="/wiki/Iditarod_Trail_Sled_Dog_Race" title="Iditarod Trail Sled Dog Race">Iditarod Trail Sled Dog Race</a> that starts in Anchorage and ends in Nome, World Ice Art Championships in Fairbanks, the Blueberry Festival and Alaska Hummingbird Festival in <a href="/wiki/Ketchikan,_Alaska" title="Ketchikan, Alaska">Ketchikan</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sitka_Whale_Fest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sitka Whale Fest (page does not exist)">Sitka Whale Fest</a>, and the Stikine River Garnet Fest in <a href="/wiki/Wrangell,_Alaska" title="Wrangell, Alaska">Wrangell</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Stikine_River" title="Stikine River">Stikine River</a> attracts the largest springtime concentration of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_bald_eagle" title="American bald eagle">American bald eagles</a> in the world.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Native_Heritage_Center" title="Alaska Native Heritage Center">Alaska Native Heritage Center</a> celebrates the rich heritage of Alaska\'s 11 cultural groups. Their purpose is to encourage cross-cultural exchanges among all people and enhance self-esteem among Native people. The <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Native_Arts_Foundation" title="Alaska Native Arts Foundation">Alaska Native Arts Foundation</a> promotes and markets Native art from all regions and cultures in the State, using the internet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Alaska" title="Music of Alaska">Music of Alaska</a></div>\n<p>Influences on music in Alaska include the traditional music of Alaska Natives as well as folk music brought by later immigrants from Russia and Europe. Prominent musicians from Alaska include singer <a href="/wiki/Jewel_(singer)" title="Jewel (singer)">Jewel</a>, traditional Aleut flautist <a href="/wiki/Mary_Youngblood" title="Mary Youngblood">Mary Youngblood</a>, folk singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Libby_Roderick" title="Libby Roderick">Libby Roderick</a>, Christian music singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Brewster" title="Lincoln Brewster">Lincoln Brewster</a>, metal/post hardcore band <a href="/wiki/36_Crazyfists" title="36 Crazyfists">36 Crazyfists</a> and the groups <a href="/wiki/Pamyua" title="Pamyua">Pamyua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal._The_Man" title="Portugal. The Man">Portugal. The Man</a>.\n</p><p>There are many established music festivals in Alaska, including the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Folk_Festival" title="Alaska Folk Festival">Alaska Folk Festival</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fairbanks_Summer_Arts_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fairbanks Summer Arts Festival (page does not exist)">Fairbanks Summer Arts Festival</a>, the <a class="external text" href="http://anchoragefolkfestival.org/" rel="nofollow">Anchorage Folk Festival</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athabascan_Old-Time_Fiddling_Festival" title="Athabascan Old-Time Fiddling Festival">Athabascan Old-Time Fiddling Festival</a>, the Sitka Jazz Festival, and the <a href="/wiki/Sitka_Summer_Music_Festival" title="Sitka Summer Music Festival">Sitka Summer Music Festival</a>. The most prominent orchestra in Alaska is the <a href="/wiki/Anchorage_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Anchorage Symphony Orchestra">Anchorage Symphony Orchestra</a>, though the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fairbanks_Symphony_Orchestra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fairbanks Symphony Orchestra (page does not exist)">Fairbanks Symphony Orchestra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juneau_Symphony" title="Juneau Symphony">Juneau Symphony</a> are also notable. The <a href="/wiki/Anchorage_Opera" title="Anchorage Opera">Anchorage Opera</a> is currently the state\'s only professional opera company, though there are several volunteer and semi-professional organizations in the state as well.\n</p><p>The official <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_songs" title="List of U.S. state songs">state song</a> of Alaska is "<a href="/wiki/Alaska%27s_Flag" title="Alaska\'s Flag">Alaska\'s Flag</a>", which was adopted in 1955; it celebrates the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Alaska" title="Flag of Alaska">flag of Alaska</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alaska_in_film_and_on_television">Alaska in film and on television</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_in_Alaska" title="List of films set in Alaska">List of films set in Alaska</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bow_bow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1540" data-file-width="1027" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bow_bow.jpg/170px-Bow_bow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bow_bow.jpg/255px-Bow_bow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bow_bow.jpg/340px-Bow_bow.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bow_bow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Films featuring Alaskan wolves usually employ domesticated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wolf-dog_hybrid" title="Wolf-dog hybrid">wolf-dog hybrids</a> to stand in for wild wolves.</div></div></div>\n<p>Alaska\'s first independent picture entirely made in Alaska was <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chechahcos" title="The Chechahcos">The Chechahcos</a></i>, produced by Alaskan businessman <a href="/wiki/Austin_E._Lathrop" title="Austin E. Lathrop">Austin E. Lathrop</a> and filmed in and around Anchorage. Released in 1924 by the Alaska Moving Picture Corporation, it was the only film the company made.\n</p><p>One of the most prominent movies filmed in Alaska is <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">MGM</a>\'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eskimo/Mala_The_Magnificent" title="Eskimo/Mala The Magnificent">Eskimo/Mala The Magnificent</a></i>, starring Alaska Native <a href="/wiki/Ray_Mala" title="Ray Mala">Ray Mala</a>. In 1932 an expedition set out from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MGM" title="MGM">MGM</a>\'s studios in Hollywood to Alaska to film what was then billed as "The Biggest Picture Ever Made". Upon arriving in Alaska, they set up "Camp Hollywood" in Northwest Alaska, where they lived during the duration of the filming. <a href="/wiki/Louis_B._Mayer" title="Louis B. Mayer">Louis B. Mayer</a> spared no expense in spite of the remote location, going so far as to hire the chef from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Hotel_(Hollywood)" title="Roosevelt Hotel (Hollywood)">Hotel Roosevelt</a> in Hollywood to prepare meals.\n</p><p>When <i>Eskimo</i> premiered at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astor_Theatre,_New_York_City" title="Astor Theatre, New York City">Astor Theatre</a> in New York City, the studio received the largest amount of feedback in its history to that point. <i>Eskimo</i> was critically acclaimed and released worldwide; as a result, Mala became an international movie star. <i>Eskimo</i> won the first Oscar for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Film_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Film Editing">Best Film Editing</a> at the Academy Awards, and showcased and preserved aspects of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inupiat_people" title="Inupiat people">Inupiat</a> culture on film.\n</p><p>The 1983 Disney movie <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Cry_Wolf_(film)" title="Never Cry Wolf (film)">Never Cry Wolf</a></i> was at least partially shot in Alaska. The 1991 film <i><a href="/wiki/White_Fang_(1991_film)" title="White Fang (1991 film)">White Fang</a></i>, based on <a href="/wiki/Jack_London" title="Jack London">Jack London</a>\'s novel and starring <a href="/wiki/Ethan_Hawke" title="Ethan Hawke">Ethan Hawke</a>, was filmed in and around <a href="/wiki/Haines,_Alaska" title="Haines, Alaska">Haines</a>. <a href="/wiki/Steven_Seagal" title="Steven Seagal">Steven Seagal</a>\'s 1994 <i><a href="/wiki/On_Deadly_Ground" title="On Deadly Ground">On Deadly Ground</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a>, was filmed in part at the <a href="/wiki/Worthington_Glacier" title="Worthington Glacier">Worthington Glacier</a> near <a href="/wiki/Valdez,_Alaska" title="Valdez, Alaska">Valdez</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> The 1999 <a href="/wiki/John_Sayles" title="John Sayles">John Sayles</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Limbo_(1999_film)" title="Limbo (1999 film)">Limbo</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/David_Strathairn" title="David Strathairn">David Strathairn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Elizabeth_Mastrantonio" title="Mary Elizabeth Mastrantonio">Mary Elizabeth Mastrantonio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kristofferson" title="Kris Kristofferson">Kris Kristofferson</a>, was filmed in Juneau.\n</p><p>The psychological thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Insomnia_(2002_film)" title="Insomnia (2002 film)">Insomnia</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Al_Pacino" title="Al Pacino">Al Pacino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robin_Williams" title="Robin Williams">Robin Williams</a>, was shot in Canada, but was set in Alaska. The 2007 film directed by Sean Penn, <i><a href="/wiki/Into_the_Wild_(film)" title="Into the Wild (film)">Into The Wild</a></i>, was partially filmed and set in Alaska. The film, which is based on the novel of the same name, follows the adventures of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_McCandless" title="Christopher McCandless">Christopher McCandless</a>, who died in a remote abandoned bus along the <a href="/wiki/Stampede_Trail" title="Stampede Trail">Stampede Trail</a> west of <a href="/wiki/Healy,_Alaska" title="Healy, Alaska">Healy</a> in 1992.\n</p><p>Many films and television shows set in Alaska are not filmed there; for example, <i><a href="/wiki/Northern_Exposure" title="Northern Exposure">Northern Exposure</a></i>, set in the fictional town of Cicely, Alaska, was filmed in <a href="/wiki/Roslyn,_Washington" title="Roslyn, Washington">Roslyn, Washington</a>. The 2007 horror feature <i><a href="/wiki/30_Days_of_Night_(film)" title="30 Days of Night (film)">30 Days of Night</a></i> is set in <a href="/wiki/Utqiagvik,_Alaska" title="Utqiagvik, Alaska">Barrow, Alaska</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-namechange_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-namechange-133">[note 1]</a></sup>, but was filmed in New Zealand.\n</p><p>Many <a href="/wiki/Reality_television" title="Reality television">reality television</a> shows are filmed in Alaska. In 2011 the <i>Anchorage Daily News</i> found ten set in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hopkins20110214_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-hopkins20110214-134">[132]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="State_symbols">State symbols</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Alaska_state_symbols" title="List of Alaska state symbols">List of Alaska state symbols</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1137" data-file-width="1323" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg/220px-2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg/330px-2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg/440px-2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-05-04_at_18-26-44-Forgetmenot-Flower.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forget-me-not" title="Forget-me-not">forget-me-not</a> is the state\'s official flower and bears the same blue and gold as the state flag.</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>State motto: North to the Future</li>\n<li>Nicknames: "The Last Frontier" or "Land of the Midnight Sun" or "Seward\'s Icebox"</li>\n<li>State bird: <a href="/wiki/Willow_ptarmigan" title="Willow ptarmigan">willow ptarmigan</a>, adopted by the Territorial Legislature in 1955. It is a small (15&#8211;17&#160;in or 380&#8211;430&#160;mm) Arctic grouse that lives among willows and on open tundra and muskeg. Plumage is brown in summer, changing to white in winter. The willow ptarmigan is common in much of Alaska.</li>\n<li>State fish: <a href="/wiki/Chinook_salmon" title="Chinook salmon">king salmon</a>, adopted 1962.</li>\n<li>State flower: wild/native <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forget-me-not" title="Forget-me-not">forget-me-not</a>, adopted by the Territorial Legislature in 1917.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> It is a perennial that is found throughout Alaska, from Hyder to the Arctic Coast, and west to the Aleutians.</li>\n<li>State fossil: <a href="/wiki/Woolly_mammoth" title="Woolly mammoth">woolly mammoth</a>, adopted 1986.</li>\n<li>State gem: <a href="/wiki/Nephrite" title="Nephrite">jade</a>, adopted 1968.</li>\n<li>State insect: <a href="/wiki/Four-spotted_chaser" title="Four-spotted chaser">four-spot skimmer</a> dragonfly, adopted 1995.</li>\n<li>State land mammal: <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a>, adopted 1998.</li>\n<li>State marine mammal: <a href="/wiki/Bowhead_whale" title="Bowhead whale">bowhead whale</a>, adopted 1983.</li>\n<li>State mineral: <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, adopted 1968.</li>\n<li>State song: "<a href="/wiki/Alaska%27s_Flag" title="Alaska\'s Flag">Alaska\'s Flag</a>"</li>\n<li>State sport: <a href="/wiki/Mushing" title="Mushing">dog mushing</a>, adopted 1972.</li>\n<li>State tree: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sitka_spruce" title="Sitka spruce">Sitka spruce</a>, adopted 1962.</li>\n<li>State dog: <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Malamute" title="Alaskan Malamute">Alaskan Malamute</a>, adopted 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup></li>\n<li>State soil: <a href="/wiki/Tanana_(soil)" title="Tanana (soil)">Tanana</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> adopted unknown.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See portal</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Index_of_Alaska-related_articles" title="Index of Alaska-related articles">Index of Alaska-related articles</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Alaska" class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-108">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Byron_Mallott" title="Byron Mallott">Byron Mallott</a>, the Democratic gubernatorial nominee, suspended his campaign and became the running mate of <a href="/wiki/Bill_Walker_(American_politician)" title="Bill Walker (American politician)">Bill Walker</a>, an independent who left the Republican Party.
